A.3.2 - A1 - Core Stability Parameters - Role Of Stability Facilitators Core Stability Parameters - Role Of Stability Facilitators Section This Section defines the role of the Stability Facilitators in managing the Core Stability Parameters.
A.3.2 - Core Stability Parameters - Role Of Stability Facilitators - Broad Authority Core Stability Parameters - Role Of Stability Facilitators - Broad Authority Core Prior to the launch of Star Vaults and the implementation of a new Rate System, all Stability Parameters related to Sky Core and Spark Star will be managed by the Stability Facilitators, in consultation with the Stability Scope Advisors. This process will be conducted through the Operational Weekly Governance Cycle or, if necessary, through out-of-schedule Executive Votes.
A.3.2 - Core Stability Parameters - Role Of Stability Facilitators - Spark Protocol Debt Ceiling Core Stability Parameters - Role Of Stability Facilitators - Spark Protocol Debt Ceiling Core As long as Spark Protocol remains near its maximum borrow limit, the Stability Facilitators can use the Operational Weekly Governance Cycle to propose to increase its Debt Ceiling to attract more users.
A.3.2 - A2 - Core Stability Parameters - Parameters Core Stability Parameters - Parameters Section This Section defines the Core Stability Parameters.
A.3.2 - Core Stability Parameters - Parameters - Base Rate Core Stability Parameters - Parameters - Base Rate Core The Base Rate is the key interest rate in the system. It defines all other rates by various spreads. It is expressed as an annual percentage rate.
A.3.2 - Core Stability Parameters - Parameters - Long Term Base Rate Determination Process Core Stability Parameters - Parameters - Long Term Base Rate Determination Process Core In the long term, the Base Rate must be automatically determined based on a model which ensures long term price stability of USDS and other Stablecoins produced by the Sky Ecosystem.
A.3.2 - Core Stability Parameters - Parameters - Medium Term Base Rate Determination Process Core Stability Parameters - Parameters - Medium Term Base Rate Determination Process Core In the medium term, the Base Rate is changed by Executive Votes proposed by the Stability Facilitators based on the recommendation of the Stability Scope Advisors.The Stability Facilitators must regularly update the Base Rate in order to ensure (1) a sufficient level of Cash Stablecoins and (2) price stability of USDS and other Stablecoins produced by the Ecosystem.
A.3.2 - Core Stability Parameters - Parameters - Base Rate Spread Determination Process Core Stability Parameters - Parameters - Base Rate Spread Determination Process Core Spreads which are attached to the Base Rate can also be changed through the Operational Weekly Governance Cycle.
A.3.2 - Core Stability Parameters - Parameters - Dai Savings Rate Core Stability Parameters - Parameters - Dai Savings Rate Core The Dai Savings Rate ("DSR") is the rate Dai holders can earn on their Dai in the Dai Savings Rate smart contracts.
A.3.2 - Core Stability Parameters - Parameters - Dai Savings Rate Formula Core Stability Parameters - Parameters - Dai Savings Rate Formula Core The Dai Savings Rate is determined based on the Base Rate and DSR Spread parameter using the following formula:Dai Savings Rate = Base Rate + DSR Spread
A.3.2 - Core Stability Parameters - Parameters - Dai Savings Rate Current Value Core Stability Parameters - Parameters - Dai Savings Rate Current Value Core The current value of the Dai Savings Rate is 5.5%.
A.3.2 - Core Stability Parameters - Parameters - Sky Savings Rate Core Stability Parameters - Parameters - Sky Savings Rate Core The Sky Savings Rate ("SSR") is the rate USDS holders can earn on their USDS in the Sky Savings Rate smart contracts.
A.3.2 - Core Stability Parameters - Parameters - Sky Savings Rate Formula Core Stability Parameters - Parameters - Sky Savings Rate Formula Core The Sky Savings Rate is determined based on the Dai Savings Rate and the USDS Spread parameter using the following formula:Sky Savings Rate = Dai Savings Rate + USDS Spread
A.3.2 - Core Stability Parameters - Parameters - USDS Spread Current Value Core Stability Parameters - Parameters - USDS Spread Current Value Core The current value of the USDS Spread is 1%.
A.3.2 - Core Stability Parameters - Parameters - Stars Credit Line Borrow Rate Core Stability Parameters - Parameters - Stars Credit Line Borrow Rate Core The Stars Credit Line Borrow Rate is the annual percentage rate that Stars must pay to Sky Core to receive USDS liquidity into their respective vaults.
A.3.2 - Core Stability Parameters - Parameters - Stars Credit Line Borrow Rate Risk Limits Core Stability Parameters - Parameters - Stars Credit Line Borrow Rate Risk Limits Core USDS liquidity that Stars receive from Sky Core can be deployed across Conduits within risk limits defined by the Stability Facilitators.
A.3.3 - A1 - Real World Assets - Arranged Structures Real World Assets - Arranged Structures Section Arranged Structures are special legal structures set up by Ecosystem Actors to secure Real World Assets to help stabilize the Sky Ecosystem. Each Arranged Structure has a Conduit system which is owned by a Star and automatically connected to all Stars; the Conduit allows them to send and receive USDS or other assets.
A.3.3 - A2 - Real World Assets - Star Owner For Arranged Structures Real World Assets - Star Owner For Arranged Structures Section Arranged Structures must have a Star owner. The Star owner assigns instructions to the Arranged Structure on behalf of Sky, and determines if and how other Stars can access the Conduit of the Arranged Structure.
A.3.3 - A3 - Real World Assets - Arrangers Real World Assets - Arrangers Section This Section defines procedures related to Arrangers, Ecosystem Actors that assist in the design and operation of Arranged Structures. Every Arranged Structure must have a designated Arranger responsible for conducting ongoing reporting. All aspects of this relationship, including the Arranger's duties, must be defined in this Section.
A.3.3 - Real World Assets - Arrangers - Introduction Real World Assets - Arrangers - Introduction Core Arrangers are Ecosystem Actors who specialize in sourcing, negotiating, structuring, and reporting on Real World Assets, as well as maintaining and monitoring the underlying Arranged Structures used by the Sky Protocol. The Arrangers manage a restricted function on the Arranged Structure Conduit that allows them to send assets onwards to the predetermined blockchain account of the Arranged Structure.Arrangers are generally prohibited from occupying any position where they could cause damage or loss to the Sky Ecoystem, notwithstanding delays or inconveniences.After the Arranged Structures are established and assets are allocated, Arrangers must not have the capability to operate or influence the legal and operational structure's asset operations in any manner that could cause significant harm or losses to the stability of USDS. Arrangers are directly approved by SKY voters, and all LRA collateral exposure must be structured by an approved Arranger.
A.3.3 - Real World Assets - Arrangers - Onboarding And Offboarding of Arrangers Real World Assets - Arrangers - Onboarding And Offboarding of Arrangers Core When they deem it necessary, the Stability Facilitators may initiate a Governance Poll to onboard or offboard Arrangers. The list of current active Arrangers is maintained in A.3.3 - Real World Assets - Arrangers - List Of Active Arrangers.
A.3.3 - Real World Assets - Arrangers - List Of Active Arrangers Real World Assets - Arrangers - List Of Active Arrangers Core List of current active Arrangers:• BlocktowerFollowing the voluntary offboarding of Monetalis as an active Arranger, the Clydesdale RWA Arranged Structure must be wound down by the Stability Facilitator in collaboration with Monetalis or another suitable entity that can serve as an interim Arranger. This process must ensure a smooth and orderly wind-down of the assets within Clydesdale to minimize fees and maximize returns.
A.3.3 - Real World Assets - Arrangers - Reporting And Stress Test Requirements Real World Assets - Arrangers - Reporting And Stress Test Requirements Core Arrangers must publish monthly reporting on each Arranged Structure they have arranged. Every six (6) months, Arrangers are also required to publish a stress test analysis that demonstrates how the structures would perform under historical financial crisis scenarios and other hypothetical scenarios.The Stability Facilitators must periodically fund independent Ecosystem Actors to review and verify the quality and the results of the stress tests. Should an independent review produce an unfavorable result, the Stability Facilitators must propose a Governance Poll for warning, temporarily deactivating, or permanently offboarding the Arranger and/or the Asset Managers connected to the discovered issue.To be considered compliant, Arrangers' monthly reports must satisfy the requirements of one of the following documents:•A.3.3 - Real World Assets - Arrangers - Monthly Arranger Report Requirements• A.3.3 - Real World Assets - Arrangers - Access To Accounts
A.3.3 - Real World Assets - Arrangers - Monthly Arranger Report Requirements Real World Assets - Arrangers - Monthly Arranger Report Requirements Core The following information must be included in the monthly Arranger report. Each item must be reported for at least the start and end date of the reporting period. If these dates fall on days when markets are closed, the first business day after the start date and the last business day before the end date may be used instead.• Cash balance.• Cash income over the reporting period. Any income over $20,000 in value should be broken out as its own line item, and an explanation provided for any non-recurring or non-ordinary expenses.• Cash expenses over the reporting period. Any expense over $20,000 in value should be broken out as its own line item, and an explanation provided for any non-recurring or non-ordinary expenses.• Market value of publicly traded equities, ETFs, and mutual funds.• Market value (the closing price) of publicly traded debt securities. Debt securities that are investment grade and less than 12 months from maturity may alternatively be reported at cost basis + linearly recognizing scheduled interest income.• A valuation for illiquid or privately traded assets. This should utilize a valuation from a reputable third party with relevant expertise or follow a well-defined methodology that is explained in detail in the report.• CUSIPs, date of purchase, date of maturity, coupon, cost basis, and face value of all publicly traded debt securities in the portfolio for the last day of the reporting period.• USDS inflows from the Sky Protocol during the reporting period.• Total repayments on-chain to the Sky Protocol either to a vault or for surplus. If repayments are derived from multiple sources, they should be broken out into line items for each source.• Vault debt to the Sky Protocol.• Copies of original statements for all bank, brokerage, exchange, custodial, or other accounts. The Arranger may redact the names for non-Arranger service providers if and only if that is a requirement of confidentiality agreements with the non-Arranger service providers.The Stability Facilitator must publicly confirm on the Sky Forum that they have reviewed the original account documentation and verified that it supports the Arranger's summary.
A.3.3 - Real World Assets - Arrangers - Access To Accounts Real World Assets - Arrangers - Access To Accounts Core As an alternative to the requirements set out in A.3.3 - Real World Assets - Arrangers - Monthly Arranger Report Requirements, the Arranger can provide the following information through public read-only access to all accounts:• All asset balances• All transaction amounts (non-Arranger service provider names may be redacted)• Hold-to-maturity yields (for assets with maturity) or current yield (for assets with no maturity)In addition, Makerburn.com (https://makerburn.com/#/), Daistats.com (https://daistats.com/#/), or another dashboard must be publicly available to summarize USDS inflows and outflows from the Sky vault.
A.3.3 - A4 - Real World Assets - Star Owner Can Change Arrangers Real World Assets - Star Owner Can Change Arrangers Section The Star owner of the Arranged Structure can change the blockchain account of the Arranged Structure and change the Arranger.
A.3.3 - A5 - Real World Assets - Perpetual Yield Strategies Real World Assets - Perpetual Yield Strategies Section The subdocuments herein define perpetual yield strategies and exposure targets that can be implemented by the Stability Facilitators.
A.3.3 - Real World Assets - Perpetual Yield Strategies - Implemented By Stability Facilitator Real World Assets - Perpetual Yield Strategies - Implemented By Stability Facilitator Core The Stability Facilitators can implement various perpetual yield strategies, including on-chain and off-chain mechanisms, that enable the Sky Protocol to take advantage of high risk-adjusted return on perpetual yield strategies in the crypto markets. Exposure targets specified in this document override requirements defined by other Articles of the Stability Scope.
A.3.3 - Real World Assets - Perpetual Yield Strategies - Perpetual Exposure Real World Assets - Perpetual Yield Strategies - Perpetual Exposure Core The subdocuments herein define Perpetual Exposure parameters and the associated governance processes.
A.3.3 - Real World Assets - Perpetual Yield Strategies - Perpetual Exposure Direct Accumulation Real World Assets - Perpetual Yield Strategies - Perpetual Exposure Direct Accumulation Core The Stability Facilitators can trigger Executive Votes that instruct Arranged Structures to set up mechanisms that allow them to take direct exposure to Ethena sUSDe, or use legal rails to get direct exposure through custodians.
A.3.3 - Real World Assets - Perpetual Yield Strategies - Adjustment Of Perpetual Exposure Direct Accumulation Real World Assets - Perpetual Yield Strategies - Adjustment Of Perpetual Exposure Direct Accumulation Active Data Controller The level of exposure that can be adjusted is defined as Active Data in: A.3.3 - Real World Assets - Perpetual Yield Strategies - Andromeda Direct Exposure A.3.3 - Real World Assets - Perpetual Yield Strategies - Clydesdale Legal Rails Exposure A.3.3 - Real World Assets - Perpetual Yield Strategies - Andromeda Legal Rails ExposureThe Active Data is updated as follows:• The Responsible Party is the Stability Facilitators.• The Update Process must follow the protocol for 'Direct Edit'.
A.3.3 - Real World Assets - Perpetual Yield Strategies - Requirements For Adjustment Of Perpetual Exposure Direct Accumulation Real World Assets - Perpetual Yield Strategies - Requirements For Adjustment Of Perpetual Exposure Direct Accumulation Core When updating the Active Data controlled by A.3.3 - Real World Assets - Perpetual Yield Strategies - Adjustment Of Perpetual Exposure Direct Accumulation, the Stability Facilitators shall consult with the Stability Scope Advisors and other recognized Ecosystem Actors.
A.3.3 - Real World Assets - Perpetual Yield Strategies - Morpho Vaults Real World Assets - Perpetual Yield Strategies - Morpho Vaults Core The subdocuments herein define the exposure for the Morpho Vaults and the associated governance processes.
A.3.3 - Real World Assets - Perpetual Yield Strategies - Morpho Overcollateralized SUSDe Or USDe DDM Real World Assets - Perpetual Yield Strategies - Morpho Overcollateralized SUSDe Or USDe DDM Core The Stability Facilitators can trigger Executive Votes that set up DDMs to Morpho Vaults that have overcollateralized exposure to sUSDe or USDe.
A.3.3 - Real World Assets - Perpetual Yield Strategies - Adjustment Of Exposure Morpho Vault Real World Assets - Perpetual Yield Strategies - Adjustment Of Exposure Morpho Vault Active Data Controller The level of exposure is defined as Active Data in A.3.3 - Real World Assets - Perpetual Yield Strategies - Current Exposure Of Morpho SUSDe Or USDe DDM Vault. A.3.3 - Real World Assets - Perpetual Yield Strategies - Morpho Vault Multisig Real World Assets - Perpetual Yield Strategies - Morpho Vault Multisig Core A multisig, controlled by Governance Facilitator JanSky, has been established to adjust the DDM parameters in real time. To prevent abuse, the management of the DDM parameters, and Governance Facilitator JanSky's use of the multisig, must wholly adhere to the Stability Facilitator's instructions, as required by A.3.3 - Real World Assets - Perpetual Yield Strategies - Management Of Morpho Vault. A.3.4 - A1 - Collateral Portfolio Collateral Portfolio Section This Section governs the management of Sky's Collateral Portfolio.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Stablecoin Collateral Reserve Collateral Portfolio - Stablecoin Collateral Reserve Core Sky must maintain a reserve of at least 20% of the total Dai and USDS Supply held as Cash Stablecoins, or assets and exposure that can rapidly be converted to Cash Stablecoins.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Cash Stablecoin Definition And List Collateral Portfolio - Cash Stablecoin Definition And List Core A Cash Stablecoin is defined as either a Stablecoin listed in A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - List Of Cash Stablecoin; a technically secure DeFi token that can be instantly converted to a listed Stablecoin; or a custody solution that can be converted into a listed Stablecoin within 30 minutes. The Stability Facilitators can modify the above cited document through the Operational Weekly Governance Cycle to react to changing market conditions, opportunities or risks. The modification of the list can include adding or removing Cash Stablecoins, or changing the terms of existing Cash Stablecoins on the list.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - List Of Cash Stablecoin Collateral Portfolio - List Of Cash Stablecoin Core List of Cash Stablecoins:• USDC and USDC in Coinbase Custody
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Stablecoin Collateral Reserve - Cash Stablecoin Peg Stability Module Upgrades Collateral Portfolio - Stablecoin Collateral Reserve - Cash Stablecoin Peg Stability Module Upgrades Core The mechanism for holding and making Cash Stablecoins available to support the liquidity of Dai and USDS can be upgraded to a superior technical, financial or legal solution by a proposal from the Stability Facilitators through the Operational Weekly Governance Cycle.The Stability Facilitators may specify requirements for how Star Advisory teams deploy USDS generated from their Star Vault.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Asset Liability Management Collateral Portfolio - Asset Liability Management Core To ensure adequate liquidity, Cash Stablecoins are managed through a simple Asset Liability Management framework. This framework allocates excess Cash Stablecoins into low-risk RWA assets, and draws on these assets to replenish the Cash Stablecoins when they fall too low.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Asset Liability Management - Excess Cash Stablecoins Collateral Portfolio - Asset Liability Management - Excess Cash Stablecoins Core If the Dai and USDS Collateral portfolio contains more than 30% of Cash Stablecoins as defined above, then any Cash Stablecoins above the 30% mark must be allocated towards the collateral defined in A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Asset Liability Management - Low Risk RWA.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Asset Liability Management - Lack Of Cash Stablecoins Collateral Portfolio - Asset Liability Management - Lack Of Cash Stablecoins Core If the Dai and USDS Collateral portfolio contains less than 20% Cash Stablecoins, the assets defined in A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Asset Liability Management - Low Risk RWA must be sold off to return the Cash Stablecoin exposure to 25%.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Asset Liability Management - Low Risk RWA Collateral Portfolio - Asset Liability Management - Low Risk RWA Core Andromeda is the RWA Arranged Structure that can allocate capital into Low-Risk RWA (LRR). LRR is safe, short-term treasury strategies of less than one (1) year duration. Whenever excess Cash Stablecoins must be allocated into LRR, or whenever LRR must be sold to replenish Cash Stablecoins, the amounts allocated or sold are applied to the Andromeda RWA Arranged Structure.Control of the Andromeda RWA Arranged Structure must be prepared to transition to the Spark Star.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Asset Liability Management - Optimizations Collateral Portfolio - Asset Liability Management - Optimizations Core The Stability Facilitators can use the Operational Weekly Governance Cycle to modify the Asset Liability Management framework in order to make it more efficient, or more resilient. This modification can involve changing any of the logic defined in A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Asset Liability Management or its subdocuments.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Legacy RWA Offboarding Collateral Portfolio - Legacy RWA Offboarding Core Old RWA exposure that was added before Endgame must stay for as long as necessary, and optimized for yield if possible. When it is possible, the Stability Facilitators should take action to wind down and offboard all Legacy RWA. Governance actions related to optimizations, wind down and offboardings can be done directly in Executive Votes with no prior Governance Poll needed.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process Core The subdocuments herein define the process by which Sky vault users should be notified about collateral offboarding.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Legacy Context Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Legacy Context Core Periodically, collateral and vault types (ilks) are re-evaluated, which sometimes results in an offboarding of that collateral or vault type. There have been several instances where users entered official Sky forums/chats to understand why they had been suddenly liquidated, despite historically comfortable collateralization ratios (https://forum.makerdao.com/t/an-assessment-first-hand-experience-and-recommendations-from-the-aave-offboarding/11836). This is, understandably, a poor user experience. Even with liquidation penalties set to 0%, the forced unwinding of levered positions conceivably can result in user losses, as well as potentially taxable events. This Section defines procedures concerning the dissemination of information about upcoming collateral offboarding on a best-effort basis. The objective is to minimize the number of users who are unaware of the offboarding prior to getting their positions liquidated.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Legacy Context Specific Goals Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Legacy Context Specific Goals Core Specific Goals:1. Codify a series of good-faith communication efforts.2. Provide an easy-to-follow process for Sky contributors to follow without significant burden.3. Minimize the number of users unaware of a collateral offboarding.4. Provide a method to bypass these requirements in the event a collateral is being offboarded due to serious security or solvency concerns.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Technical Process Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Technical Process Core The subdocuments herein specify actions to be taken by specific actors within Sky when offboarding a vault type.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Immediate Actions Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Immediate Actions Core Upon approval by Sky Governance to offboard a permissionless collateral type or vault type, the following actions are taken as soon as is practicable:• Set debt ceiling to zero (0) Dai or USDS.• Make an initial public announcement on all communication channels listed in A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Communication Channels And Media Assets Listing.• Make a second public announcement on all communication channels in the above cited document no later than 14 calendar days after the initial public announcement.• Once the second public announcements have been made, set the liquidation penalty to 0%.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Following Actions Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Following Actions Core Parameter changes designed to offboard users, such as changes to the liquidation ratio or stability fee, can only be implemented once 14 calendar days have passed following a second public announcement.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Communication Channels And Media Assets Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Communication Channels And Media Assets Active Data Controller The process for adding, removing, and modifying communication channels and media assets, and the order of announcement publication, are defined as Active Data in A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Communication Channels And Media Assets Listing.The Active Data is updated as follows:• The Responsible Party is the Communication Coordinator.• The Update Process must follow the protocol for 'Direct Edit'.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Communication Coordinator Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Communication Coordinator Core The subdocuments herein define the Communication Coordinator role.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Designated Responsible Party Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Designated Responsible Party Core The Communication Coordinator is designated the Responsible Party who is authorized to modify the Active Data document at A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Communication Channels And Media Assets Listing.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - The Current Communication Coordinator Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - The Current Communication Coordinator Active Data Controller The current Communication Coordinator is defined as Active Data in A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Current Communication Coordinator. The Active Data is updated as follows:• The Responsible Party is the Governance Facilitators. • The Update Process must follow the protocol for 'Direct Edit' and must adhere to the additional requirements defined in A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Requirements For Modification Of Current Communication Coordinator.

A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Expedited Offboarding Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Expedited Offboarding Core The subdocuments herein define an expedited offboarding process in the event a collateral type needs to be removed quickly due to security or solvency concerns.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Requirements Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Requirements Core When a collateral type threatens the security or solvency of the Sky Protocol, an expedited offboarding is in order. Expedited offboardings override the timeline specified in A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Technical Process and allow the immediate modification of all relevant parameters.Expedited offboardings must proceed pursuant to the following requirements:• The Offboarding Proposal must state that the offboarding should be expedited due to an emergency or urgent concern, as defined in A.1.14 - A1 - Emergency Voting System.• Explicitly and clearly reference this Atlas document.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Announcements Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Announcements Core The public announcements defined in A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Offboarding Process - Technical Process must still be carried out. However, the timing of these announcements no longer constrains the modification of parameters. These announcements must also state that the offboarding is being expedited and explain the reasons for this accelerated process.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module Core A Peg Stability Module ("PSM") allows users to swap a given collateral type directly for Dai or USDS at a fixed rate, rather than borrowing Dai or USDS. The PSM contract was designed with Stablecoin collateral in mind, allowing users to swap other Stablecoins for Dai or USDS at a fixed rate to aid with keeping Dai or USDS pegged to one (1) USD.A PSM operates similarly to a regular vault type with a zero Stability Fee and a liquidation ratio of 100% that can only be accessed through a user-facing smart contract containing the relevant swap functions. Unlike regular vaults, users of the PSM do not retain ownership of the asset and borrow Dai or USDS. Instead, PSM users swap the asset directly for Dai or USDS.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - Lite Peg Stability Module Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - Lite Peg Stability Module Core The subdocuments herein manage the Lite Peg Stability Module.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - Lite Peg Stability Module Parameter Definitions Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - Lite Peg Stability Module Parameter Definitions Core The subdocuments herein define the parameters of the Lite Peg Stability Module.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - Toll / Fee In Definition Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - Toll / Fee In Definition Core tin is a percentage fee applied when trading the collateral asset into the PSM in exchange for Dai.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - Toll / Fee Out Definition Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - Toll / Fee Out Definition Core tout is the percentage fee applied when trading Dai into the PSM in exchange for the collateral asset.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - Maximum Debt Ceiling Definition Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - Maximum Debt Ceiling Definition Core DC-IAM line is the maximum amount of debt the LitePSM can accrue.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - Target Available Debt Definition Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - Target Available Debt Definition Core DC-IAM gap is the target gap between the debt usage and the Debt Ceiling.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - Ceiling Increase Cooldown Definition Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - Ceiling Increase Cooldown Definition Core DC-IAM ttl is the minimum time requirement before it is possible to increase the debt ceiling, expressed in seconds.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - Buffer Definition Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - Buffer Definition Core buf is a fixed-sized amount of pre-minted Dai which LitePSM is designed to maintain in most instances. Note, however, that when a user calls buyGem, the amount of Dai available can be temporarily larger than buf.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - Authorized Parties Definition Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - Authorized Parties Definition Core Authorized Parties are actors who are authorized by Sky Governance to use the Lite Peg Stability Module without paying swap fees.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - Lite Peg Stability Module Parameter Modification Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - Lite Peg Stability Module Parameter Modification Core The Stability Facilitators, in consultation with the Stability Scope Advisors, may recommend changes to any of the parameters specified in the subdocuments of A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - Lite Peg Stability Module Parameter Definitions. These changes will be subject to an Executive Vote through the Operational Weekly Governance Cycle.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - Lite Peg Stability Module Parameter Values Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - Lite Peg Stability Module Parameter Values Core The current values of the Lite Peg Stability Module parameters are:• tin: 0%• tout: 0%• DC-IAM line: 10,000,000,000• DC-IAM gap: 400,000,000• DC-IAM ttl: 43,200 seconds• buf: 400,000,000• Authorized Parties: None
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - Legacy Peg Stability Modules Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - Legacy Peg Stability Modules Core All other Peg Stability Modules must be offboarded when the migration to the Lite PSM is complete. This will be coordinated by the Stability Facilitators in consultation with the Stability Scope Advisors. The subdocuments herein specify the terms of legacy Peg Stability Modules. These documents become obsolete when the respective Peg Stability Modules have been offboarded.
A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - USDC PSM And Coinbase Custody Collateral Portfolio - Peg Stability Module - USDC PSM And Coinbase Custody Core Whenever the total amount of USDC in the Peg Stability Module ("PSM") plus the total amount of USDC in GUNI pools falls below 400 million, USDC must be transferred from Coinbase Custody to the PSM to bring the total amount of USDC in the PSM, plus the total amount of USDC in the GUNI pools, to 550m USDC. Whenever the total amount of USDC in the PSM, plus the total amount of USDC in GUNI pools exceeds 700 million, USDC must be transferred from the PSM to Coinbase Custody to bring the total amount of USDC in the PSM, plus the total amount of USDC in the GUNI pools, to 550m USDC. This mechanism can be fully replaced with an upgraded PSM that makes the Coinbase Custody solution obsolete. The Stability Facilitators can directly trigger an Executive Vote to implement an upgraded PSM.
A.3.5 - A1 - Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Surplus Buffer Upper Limit Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Surplus Buffer Upper Limit Section This Section defines the Surplus Buffer Upper Limit and key parameters of the Smart Burn Engine.
A.3.5 - Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters Core The amount of USDS in the Surplus Buffer that causes the Smart Burn Engine to activate, and the rate at which it uses the USDS to improve SKY liquidity, are determined by two parameters defined by the following subdocuments. The Smart Burn Engine, which defines specific parameter configuration requirements of DssFlapper, and how it should be altered are also defined in the following subdocuments.
A.3.5 - Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Upper Limit Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Upper Limit Core The Surplus Buffer Upper Limit determines the amount of USDS necessary for the Smart Burn Engine to activate.
A.3.5 - Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Upper Limit Amount Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Upper Limit Amount Core The Surplus Buffer Upper Limit is: 55 million USDS
A.3.5 - Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - SKY Accumulation Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - SKY Accumulation Core The Smart Burn Engine can switch between accumulating SKY/USDS liquidity and directly accumulating SKY only.The Stability Facilitators can trigger a switch from one mode of accumulation to the other, based on market factors and input from the Stability Scope Advisors.By default, the Smart Burn Engine must be switched to directly accumulating SKY only.
A.3.5 - Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Rate Of SKY Accumulation Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Rate Of SKY Accumulation Core The rate of SKY Accumulation should target the approximate net surplus income rate of the Sky Protocol. The Stability Facilitators must regularly update the relevant Smart Burn Engine parameters, in consultation with the Stability Scope Advisors, to ensure they continuously track the net surplus income rate.Stability Facilitators should aim to slightly underestimate the net surplus income rate. This approach allows the Surplus Buffer to slowly grow above its upper limit, while ensuring that most of the net surplus income is used by the Smart Burn Engine, Activation, and Sealing.
A.3.5 - Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - SKY Maximum Price Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - SKY Maximum Price Core If the SKY price surpasses 0.33 USD, the Smart Burn Engine must be turned off, and the Surplus Buffer Upper Limit set to infinity via an Executive Vote.
A.3.5 - Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - DssFlapper Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - DssFlapper Core DssFlapper is the current implementation of the contract which processes Smart Burn Engine transactions once activated. The DssFlapper includes the following parameters: hop, want, bump, pip and receiver. Stability Facilitators can propose DssFlapper reconfiguration within limits defined in each parameter's corresponding document. The Stability Facilitators can propose these changes directly to an Executive Vote, with the exception of the receiver and pip . These parameters always require a Governance Poll, unless the Sky Protocol is in a state of emergency, such that the expedited modification of parameters is necessary to prevent loss of funds.
A.3.5 - Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Hop Parameter Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Hop Parameter Core Flapper.hop: Minimum seconds interval between kicks.Determines maximum allowed frequency of transactions taking place.Maximum hop must be set to equal the approximate Effective Rate of MKR Accumulation defined in A.3.5 - Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters depending on the corresponding configuration of bump parameter.
A.3.5 - Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Hop Parameter Amount Of Seconds Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Hop Parameter Amount Of Seconds Core The hop parameter is: 11,635 seconds
A.3.5 - Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Want Parameter Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Want Parameter Core Flapper.want: Relative multiplier of the oracle price needed for the swap.For example, 0.98 * WAD allows for a 2% worse price than the MKR/USD reference oracle (pip) price used in the system. want must not exceed 2%.
A.3.5 - Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Want Parameter Number Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Want Parameter Number Core The want parameter is: 0.98
A.3.5 - Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Bump Parameter Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Bump Parameter Core Vow.bump: Minimum amount of Dai above Surplus Buffer Upper Limit required for eligible market transaction. bump is the amount of Dai used to get MKR. The bump should be set to minimize both price impact and transaction costs, based on an analysis of network conditions provided by the Stability Scope Advisors and the anticipated outlook for these factors.
A.3.5 - Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Bump Parameter Amount Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Bump Parameter Amount Core The bump parameter is: 25,000 DAI
A.3.5 - Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Pip Parameter Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Pip Parameter Core Flappers.pip: A reference price oracle, used for bounding the exchange rate of the swap.
A.3.5 - Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Pip Parameter Address Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Pip Parameter Address Core The pip parameter is: 0x61A12E5b1d5E9CC1302a32f0df1B5451DE6AE437
A.3.5 - Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Receiver Parameter Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Receiver Parameter Core receiver: address which will receive the Univ2 MKR/Dai LP token.
A.3.5 - Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Receiver Parameter Address Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Receiver Parameter Address Core The receiver parameter is:MCD_PAUSE_PROXY: 0xBE8E3e3618f7474F8cB1d074A26afFef007E98FB
A.3.5 - Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Parameter Reconfiguration Methodology & Frequency Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Parameter Reconfiguration Methodology & Frequency Core Via the first available Executive Vote, the Stability Facilitators must update the Smart Burn Engine Dss Flapper related parameters based on cost optimization analyses provided by the Stability Scope Advisors. Due to the volatility of market impact and gas consumption, which are key factors in cost optimization, there is no fixed frequency for these updates. The Scope Advisors are responsible for continuously monitoring the Smart Burn Engine and notifying the Stability Facilitators when changes are needed. This notification must include the relevant analysis and proposed parameter adjustments within the established limits and boundaries defined by the Stability Scope.
A.3.5 - Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Migration Surplus Buffer And Smart Burn Engine - Parameters - Migration Core The Smart Burn Engine and corresponding liquidity must be migrated to USDS/SKY when this is technically available.
A.3.7 - SKY Backstop - Emission Rate SKY Backstop - Emission Rate Section An emissions rate for the SKY backstop function that prevents risk of sudden failure must be defined. This must be continuously assessed and improved to maximize stability of the system in worst case scenarios.
A.3.7 - SKY Backstop - Emission Rate - Limitless SKY Backstop - Emission Rate - Limitless Core The SKY Backstop is temporarily limitless.
A.3.7 - SKY Backstop - Maximum Level Of Emission SKY Backstop - Maximum Level Of Emission Section A maximum level of SKY emission per undercollateralization event must be defined. This must be continuously assessed and improved to maximize stability of the system in worst-case scenarios.
A.3.7 - SKY Backstop - Override Mechanism SKY Backstop - Override Mechanism Section The Protocol must include an override mechanism that allows Sky Governance to continue emitting SKY beyond the maximum level. This Section must specify research processes and principles to guide when and how the override mechanism can be safely used.
A.3.7 - SKY Backstop - Halt Mechanism SKY Backstop - Halt Mechanism Section The Protocol must contain a SKY backstop halt mechanism that immediately halts the backstop event in case of severe risk of total failure.
A.3.7 - SKY Backstop - Mitigate Worst Case Scenario SKY Backstop - Mitigate Worst Case Scenario Section In case the backstop limit is reached and not overridden, or in case the backstop is halted during the event, the USDS target price receives a haircut to settle the remaining bad debt of the system. This Section must define elements and infrastructure to address this worst-case scenario, including research concerning ways to mitigate damage.

A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Risk Parameter Definitions Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Risk Parameter Definitions Core The Native Vault Engine risk parameters are defined in the subdocuments herein.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Liquidation Ratio Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Liquidation Ratio Core The Liquidation Ratio parameter limits the maximum amount of Dai debt that a vault user can draw from their vault given the value of their collateral locked in that vault. In practice, it expresses the minimum collateral in percentage terms that can support a given Dai debt. If the ratio of a Vault user's collateral to their debt drops below this value, their vault can be liquidated. Each vault type has its own Liquidation Ratio. The Liquidation Ratio for each vault type is expressed as a percentage value of the collateral that must be present in the vault to support its debt.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Debt Ceiling Limit Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Debt Ceiling Limit Core The Debt Ceiling Limit is numerically provided and acts as an upper limit. The Stability Facilitators can propose changes within this limit. Debt Ceiling Limit = Unlimited is defined as large enough to avoid being reached in the near future. The DC-IAM methodology contained in A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Debt Ceiling Instant Access Module (DC-IAM) acts as a risk mitigation tool. It limits the rate at which exposure can increase in a short period of time in the event of an unexpected emergency.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Stability Fee Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Stability Fee Core The Stability Fee parameter is an annual percentage fee charged on the Dai generated on Vaults. It is expressed as an annual percentage yield but it is charged on a per-block basis in Dai. The Dai from this fee is minted, added to the Dai debt for the vault, and then transferred into the Surplus Buffer which is under the control of Sky Governance. Each vault type has its own Stability Fee that can be adjusted by the Stability Facilitators. The Stability Facilitators must regularly update Vault Types' Stability Fee according to requirements defined in the subdocuments below.The Stability Scope Advisors must develop a Rate System which can be used to set various interest rates, including the rates for Core Crypto vaults and the minimum lending rate for future Stars. The Rate System must be based on external benchmarks including the risk-free rate and the highest current sustainable rate in crypto financial markets. These rates should act as the lowest and highest base rates to which additional spreads can be added to better reflect the risks involved in specific lending activities.The Rate System must be dynamic, based on the state of Cash Stablecoins in the system, and naturally move the state towards the target Cash Stablecoins defined in A.3.4 - Collateral Portfolio - Asset Liability Management.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Rates SF Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Rates SF Core ETH:• SR = 0.00%• K = 27.43%• Ka = 0.00%• Kb = 40.00%• KFa = 5.50%• KFb = 40.50%WSTETH:• SR = 0.00%• K = 12.46%• Ka = 0.00%• Kb = 20.00%• KFa = 3.50%• KFb = 7.50%WBTC:• SR = 1.00%• K = 2.65%• Ka = 3.00%• Kb = 10.00%• KFa = 3.50%• KFb = 35.50%
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Stability Fee Formulas Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Stability Fee Formulas Core List of Stability Fee Formulas according to the current conditions and chosen meta-parameters:• ETH-A: Dai Savings Rate (EDSR while active) + Normal LR Spread + Exposure Spread• ETH-B: Dai Savings Rate (EDSR while active) + Low LR Spread + Exposure Spread• ETH-C: Dai Savings Rate (EDSR while active) + High LR Spread + Exposure Spread• WSTETH-A: Dai Savings Rate (EDSR while active) + Normal LR Spread + Exposure Spread + Asset Spread• WSTETH-B: Dai Savings Rate (EDSR while active) + High LR Spread + Exposure Spread + Asset Spread• WBTC-A: Yield Collateral Yield Benchmark + Normal LR Spread + Exposure Spread• WBTC-B: Yield Collateral Yield Benchmark + Low LR Spread + Exposure Spread• WBTC-C: Yield Collateral Yield Benchmark + High LR Spread + Exposure Spread
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Spread Rates SF Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Spread Rates SF Core ETH-A Spread:• LR Spread is 0.25%• Exposure Spread is 1.49%• Asset Spread is 0.00%ETH-B Spread:• LR Spread is 0.75%• Exposure Spread is 1.49%• Asset Spread is 0.00%ETH-C Spread:• LR Spread is 0.00%• Exposure Spread is 1.49%• Asset Spread is 0.00%WSTETH-A Spread:• LR Spread is 0.25%• Exposure Spread is 1.49%• Asset Spread is 0.42%WSTETH-B Spread:• LR Spread is 0.00%• Exposure Spread is 1.49%• Asset Spread is 0.42%WBTC-A Spread:• LR Spread is 0.25%• Exposure Spread is 1.00%• Asset Spread is 0.00%WBTC-B Spread:• LR Spread is 0.75%• Exposure Spread is 1.00%• Asset Spread is 0.00%WBTC-C Spread:• LR Spread is 0.00%• Exposure Spread is 1.00%• Asset Spread is 0.00%
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Debt Ceiling Instant Access Module (DC-IAM) Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Debt Ceiling Instant Access Module (DC-IAM) Core The DC-IAM allows any user to adjust the Debt Ceiling of a supported vault type according to the rules defined in the DC-IAM smart contract logic and parameters set by the Stability Facilitators. The DC-IAM holds three parameters that can be set by Sky Governance for each vault type, (i) Maximum Debt Ceiling (line), (ii) Target Available Debt (gap), and (iii) Ceiling Increase Cooldown (ttl).
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Maximum Debt Ceiling (line) Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Maximum Debt Ceiling (line) Core The line parameter refers to the maximum value for the Debt Ceiling that the DC-IAM will allow in the given vault type. When using the DC-IAM to manage the Debt Ceiling of a vault type, the line parameter essentially replaces the Debt Ceiling parameter for that vault type. Rather than Sky Governance setting the Debt Ceiling directly, they will need to set the Maximum Debt Ceiling (line) in the DC-IAM. The line parameter is defined in Dai.The Maximum Debt Ceiling is defined in A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Debt Ceiling Limit and is currently unlimited.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Target Available Debt (gap) Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Target Available Debt (gap) Core The gap parameter controls how much of a gap the DC-IAM aims to maintain between the current debt usage and the Debt Ceiling of the vault type. The higher this value, the more risk there is from large collateral drops in very short amounts of time. The smaller this value, the more vault use is negatively affected. The gap parameter is defined in Dai.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Ceiling Increase Cooldown (ttl) Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Ceiling Increase Cooldown (ttl) Core The Ceiling Increase Cooldown (ttl) parameter controls how frequently the Debt Ceiling can be increased by the DC-IAM. If a user attempts to use the DC-IAM to increase the Debt Ceiling of a vault type before this time expires, the transaction will fail to execute and the Debt Ceiling will remain unchanged. The ttl parameter in combination with the gap parameter enforces a maximum rate at which debt usage can increase over time using a given vault type. These parameters should be set such that the maximum increase over time can accommodate all reasonable usage of the vault type in question. The ttl parameter is defined in seconds.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Auction Parameters Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Auction Parameters Core A clear justification and analysis must be provided to validate any proposed changes to the parameters specified in this document. Before these changes are added to an Executive Vote, the Stability Facilitators must first propose a Governance Poll. However, in an emergency, the Stability Facilitators have the authority to bypass the Governance Poll and add the proposed parameters directly to an Executive Vote. The parameters contained herein must be regularly monitored and updated if needed.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Auction Price Function (calc) Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Auction Price Function (calc) Core The Auction Price Function is the mathematical function that determines how the collateral price changes over time during a collateral auction. Collateral auctions use a falling price auction, where the price starts high and decreases according to the function defined in this parameter. The Exponential Stair Step function contains two key parameters, cut and step, defined in A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Auction Price Function (cut) and A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Auction Price Function (step), respectively.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Auction Price Function (cut) Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Auction Price Function (cut) Core The cut parameter controls the 'depth' of each step in the function. A smaller cut means a smoother line; a large one means more pronounced steps. The cut parameter is defined as a multiplicative factor. For example, 0.99 equated to a 1% price drop.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Auction Price Function (step) Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Auction Price Function (step) Core The step parameter controls the length of time between price drops. A smaller step means a smoother line; a large one means more pronounced steps. The step parameter is defined in seconds.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Auction Price Multiplier (buf) Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Auction Price Multiplier (buf) Core The buf parameter is a multiplier that is applied to the starting price of a collateral auction. Each vault type has its own Auction Price Multiplier that can be adjusted by Sky Governance separately. This multiplier is intended to be greater than 1.0x because Liquidations 2.0 uses falling price auctions. This means that it is generally preferable for the auction price to begin above the market price and then fall to the correct value over some amount of time. The buf parameter is defined as a multiplicative factor.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Max Auction Drawdown (cusp) Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Max Auction Drawdown (cusp) Core The Max Auction Drawdown is the maximum percentage drop in collateral price during a collateral auction before the auction is reset. 'Collateral price' in this context refers to the collateral auction price rather than the collateral market price.The Max Auction Drawdown parameter overlaps with the Max Auction Duration parameter in that an auction will need to be reset once either maximum is exceeded.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Max Auction Duration (tail) Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Max Auction Duration (tail) Core The Max Auction Duration parameter sets the maximum time that can elapse before an auction needs to reset for a particular vault type. Expressed in seconds, this parameter determines when an auction can no longer settle and must be reset.The Max Auction Duration parameter overlaps with the Max Auction Drawdown parameter in that an auction will need to be reset once either maximum is exceeded.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Proportional Kick Incentive (chip) Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Proportional Kick Incentive (chip) Core The Proportional Kick Incentive parameter represents a reward in Dai paid to the keepers that trigger collateral liquidation auctions in the Sky Protocol. The Proportional Kick Incentive is set as a percentage and represents a portion of Dai based on the debt of the vault that is being liquidated. The Dai is rewarded for each liquidation auction at the point the auction is triggered. Each vault type has its own Proportional Kick Incentive that may be adjusted separately by Sky Governance.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Flat Kick Incentive (tip) Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Flat Kick Incentive (tip) Core The Flat Kick Incentive parameter represents a reward in Dai paid to the keepers that trigger collateral liquidation auctions in the Sky Protocol. The Flat Kick Incentive is a fixed amount of Dai that is rewarded for each liquidation auction at the point the auction is triggered. Each vault type has its own Flat Kick Incentive that may be adjusted separately by Sky Governance.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Liquidation Penalty (chop) Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Liquidation Penalty (chop) Core The Liquidation Penalty parameter controls the fee vault owners must pay when their position is liquidated due to insufficient collateral. For a vault holder to receive any collateral back from the liquidations process, the debt and Liquidation Penalty must be covered by the collateral auction. Each vault type has its own Liquidation Penalty that can be adjusted by Sky Governance.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Local Liquidation Limit (hole) Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Local Liquidation Limit (hole) Core The Local Liquidation Limit sets the maximum amount of Dai debt for which collateral auctions can be active at any one time within a particular vault type. When the total Dai value of auctions exceeds this maximum for a particular vault type, no more collateral can be auctioned using that vault type until others are completed. Each vault type has a separate Local Liquidation Limit.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Debt Floor (dust) Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Debt Floor (dust) Core The Debt Floor parameter controls the minimum amount of Dai that can be minted using a specific vault type for an individual vault. If a user tries to mint Dai and the amount of Dai minted would not put the vault's amount of Dai minted above its Debt Floor, the transaction will fail and no DAi will be minted. Likewise, if a user attempts to pay back debt such that their debt will equal less than the Debt Floor and greater than zero, the transaction will fail and no Dai will be paid back. Each vault type has its own Debt Floor that can be adjusted by Sky Governance.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Collateral Offboarding Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Collateral Offboarding Core The processes for offboarding Native Vault Engine collateral are defined in the subdocuments herein.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Offboarding Low Usage Collateral Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Offboarding Low Usage Collateral Core To protect the Protocol from unnecessary complexity, the Stability Facilitators must offboard collateral types specified in A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Vault Types if they fall below a total debt of 20 million.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Offboarding WBTC Collateral Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Offboarding WBTC Collateral Core WBTC-A, WBTC-B and WBTC-C are defined in A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Vault Types only for the purpose of Stability Fee consistency. These are otherwise not considered Native Vault Engine collateral and should be offboarded according to A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Offboarding Other Collateral.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Offboarding Other Collateral Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Offboarding Other Collateral Core All other collateral types should be offboarded when the Stability Facilitators deem it appropriate and when new mechanisms are in place to take over the roles previously covered by the offboarded collateral.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Oracles Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Oracles Core The Native Vault Engine collateral types of ETH, STETH, WBTC will specifically use the Chronicle v3 oracle solution, until at least January 1st 2026. The Native Vault Engine collateral types must be migrated to the new version of the Chronicle v3 oracle when it is feasible to do so.Other oracle solutions, including diversified oracles, will only be considered until January 1st, 2026, and only if there are unresolvable security concerns with the Chronicle v3 oracles.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Updates Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Updates Core If not otherwise specified, the Stability Facilitators have the ability to trigger an Executive Vote to update any of the parameters defined in A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Risk Parameter Definitions for any of the Vault Types in A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Native Vault Engine - Vault Types.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Keepers Measures For Endgame Transition - Keepers Core Keeper networks provide critical services for the back-end systems of Sky, enhancing protocol security and efficiency. There are multiple providers of keeper networks in the Sky Ecosystem, decentralizing the keepers and ensuring redundancy. The subdocuments herein specify ongoing payment streams to compensate the different providers of keeper networks.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Keepers - Gelato Network Measures For Endgame Transition - Keepers - Gelato Network Core Gelato NetworkBudget: 1,500 USDS per dayStream Duration: 3 years (start date 29 May 2023).
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Keepers - Keep3r Network Measures For Endgame Transition - Keepers - Keep3r Network Core Keep3r NetworkBudget: 1,500 USDS per dayStream Duration: 3 years (start date 29 May 2023).
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Keepers - Chainlink Automation Measures For Endgame Transition - Keepers - Chainlink Automation Core Chainlink AutomationBudget: 1,500 USDS per dayStream Duration: 3 years (start date 29 May 2023).
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Spark Dai Direct Deposit Module Measures For Endgame Transition - Spark Dai Direct Deposit Module Core Spark is able to temporarily borrow Dai from Sky Core through the Spark Dai Direct Deposit Module (D3M).This will be replaced by borrowing at the Stars Credit Line Borrow Rate specified in A.3.2 - Core Stability Parameters - Parameters - Stars Credit Line Borrow Rate after the launch of Star Vaults and the development of a new Rate System.The Spark Dai Direct Deposit Module is managed by the Stability Facilitators, in consultation with the Stability Scope Advisors, pursuant to the subdocuments herein.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Spark Dai Direct Deposit Module - Parameter Definitions Measures For Endgame Transition - Spark Dai Direct Deposit Module - Parameter Definitions Core The subdocuments herein define the Spark Dai Direct Deposit Module parameters.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Spark Dai Direct Deposit Module - Target Available Debt Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - Spark Dai Direct Deposit Module - Target Available Debt Definition Core The gap parameter is the target gap between the debt usage and the debt ceiling.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Spark Dai Direct Deposit Module - Debt Ceiling Increase Cooldown Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - Spark Dai Direct Deposit Module - Debt Ceiling Increase Cooldown Definition Core The ttl parameter is the minimum time requirement before it is possible to increase the debt ceiling, expressed in seconds.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Spark Dai Direct Deposit Module - Maximum Debt Ceiling Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - Spark Dai Direct Deposit Module - Maximum Debt Ceiling Definition Core The line is the maximum amount of debt that can be borrowed under the Spark Dai Direct Deposit Module.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Spark Dai Direct Deposit Module - Buffer Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - Spark Dai Direct Deposit Module - Buffer Definition Core buf is a fixed-sized amount of pre-minted Dai which the Spark Dai Direct Deposit Module is designed to maintain in most instances.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Spark Dai Direct Deposit Module - Current Configuration Measures For Endgame Transition - Spark Dai Direct Deposit Module - Current Configuration Core The current parameters of the Spark Dai Direct Deposit Module are:• gap: 40 million Dai• ttl: 24 hours• max: 1.5 billion Dai• buffer: 50 million Dai
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - Spark Deployment Of New Direct Deposit Modules Measures For Endgame Transition - Spark Deployment Of New Direct Deposit Modules Core The Stability Facilitators can directly include the deployment of new Direct Deposit Modules in Executive Votes, with risk parameters defined by the Stability Facilitators. These parameters should be based on input from the Stability Scope Advisors and should best serve the needs of the Sky Ecosystem and its collaboration with other protocols.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters Core The SparkLend risk parameters are temporarily controlled by Sky Core.While the risk parameters are under the control of Sky Core, they are implemented by the Stability Facilitators in consultation with the Stability Scope Advisors, as specified in the subdocuments herein.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Definitions Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Definitions Core The subdocuments herein define the SparkLend risk parameters.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Borrow Rate Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Borrow Rate Definition Core The borrow rate is the annualized percentage yield for borrowing the asset, which is determined based on the market's Interest Rate Model and actual utilization in the market.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Supply Rate Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Supply Rate Definition Core The supply rate is the annualized percentage yield for supplying the asset, which is determined based on borrow rate as:supply rate = market utilization * borrow rate * (1-reserve factor)
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Interest Rate Model Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Interest Rate Model Definition Core The Interest Rate Model ("IRM") is defined by four main parameters:1. Base Rate - the starting rate at 0% utilization2. Variable Slope 1 - the rate at optimal utilization3. Variable Slope 2 - the rate at 100% utilization4. Utilization - the utilization itselfThe Base Rate, Slope 1, and Slope 2 parameters are further defined in:A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Base Rate Definition; A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Slope 1 Definition; and A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Slope 2 Definition.All markets except Dai use this IRM. The IRM for Dai is independent of utilization and is defined as a spread over the Core Stability Parameters Base Rate set forth in A.3.2 - Core Stability Parameters - Parameters - Base Rate. The spread is determined by the Stability Facilitators, in consultation with the Stability Scope Advisors.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - LTV Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - LTV Definition Core The LTV is the maximum percentage of the value of collateral that borrowers can borrow against their collateral.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Liquidation Threshold Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Liquidation Threshold Definition Core The liquidation threshold is the maximum debt a borrower can owe as a percentage of their collateral before their position is considered under-collateralized and thus at risk of being liquidated.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - High Efficiency Mode Category Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - High Efficiency Mode Category Definition Core The High Efficiency Mode Category groups assets that are highly correlated with each other into buckets, for example Stablecoins or various forms of ETH. Borrowing against an asset to acquire another asset in the same category can support higher LTVs and liquidation thresholds as determined by the protocol.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Liquidation Bonus Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Liquidation Bonus Definition Core The liquidation bonus is the bonus for liquidating an unhealthy loan, or equivalently the penalty for having an unhealthy loan liquidated. The party paying off the unhealthy loan is entitled to collateral with an equivalent value as the debt paid off plus the liquidation bonus.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Reserve Factor Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Reserve Factor Definition Core The reserve factor is the percentage of interest payments paid to the protocol.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Supply Cap Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Supply Cap Definition Core The supply cap is the maximum amount of the asset that can be supplied.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Borrow Cap Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Borrow Cap Definition Core The borrow cap is the maximum amount of the asset that can be borrowed.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Optimal Utilization Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Optimal Utilization Definition Core The optimal utilization represents the desired target utilization of the borrowing capacity for the asset. It is an input used to determine the interest rate of borrowing. When the actual utilization is above the optimal utilization, borrowing rates will be higher; and when the actual utilization is below the optimal utilization, borrowing rates will be lower.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Isolated Debt Ceiling Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Isolated Debt Ceiling Definition Core The isolated debt ceiling represents the maximum amount that can be borrowed against designated isolated assets, as determined by the Stability Facilitators in consultation with the Stability Scope Advisors. Only Stablecoins may be borrowed against isolated assets.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Base Rate Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Base Rate Definition Core The base rate is an input used to determine the interest rate of borrowing. The base rate is adjusted based on actual borrowing utilization relative to optimal borrowing utilization to arrive at the actual borrowing rate.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Reserve State Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Reserve State Definition Core The reserve state represents the state of the market for a particular collateral type. The reserve state may be:• Active - all activities may occur• Frozen - all activities may occur except for supplying and borrowing• Paused - no activities may occur
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Slope 1 Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Slope 1 Definition Core Slope 1 is the interest rate at optimal utilization in the Interest Rate Model.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Slope 2 Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Slope 2 Definition Core Slope 2 is the interest rate at 100% utilization in the Interest Rate Model.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Collateral-Enabled Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Collateral-Enabled Definition Core If Collateral is Enabled, then the asset may be used as collateral.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Borrowing-Enabled Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Borrowing-Enabled Definition Core If Borrowing is Enabled, then the asset may be borrowed.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Isolated Collateral-Enabled Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Isolated Collateral-Enabled Definition Core If Isolated Collateral is Enabled, only Stablecoins can be borrowed when using the asset as collateral.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Isolation Mode Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Isolation Mode Definition Core When a user is in Isolation Mode, only assets with Isolated Borrow enabled can be borrowed.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Siloed Borrowing-Enabled Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Siloed Borrowing-Enabled Definition Core If Siloed Borrowing is Enabled, then when borrowing the asset, no other asset may be borrowed.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Modification Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Modification Core The Stability Facilitators, in consultation with the Stability Scope Advisors, may recommend changes to any of the parameters specified in the subdocuments of A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Definitions or A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Cap Automator Parameter Definitions.These changes will be subject to an Executive Vote through the Weekly Governance Cycle.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Current Configuration Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Current Configuration Core The subdocuments herein define the current configuration of the SparkLend risk parameters for each collateral type.

A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Cap Automators Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Cap Automators Core Cap Automaters allow the Supply Cap defined in A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Supply Cap Definition and the Borrow Cap defined in A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Borrow Cap Definition to be dynamically adjusted.The Cap Automater is defined in terms of three parameters:1. gap - the target available exposure2. ttl - the cooldown period for cap increases3. max - the absolute maximum exposureAny user can permissionlessly update a covered Supply Cap or Borrow Cap so the available exposure is equal to the target, as long as the resulting exposure does not exceed the specified maximum limit and the cooldown period has elapsed in the case of increases to the Supply Cap or Borrow Cap.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Cap Automator Parameter Definitions Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Cap Automator Parameter Definitions Core The subdocuments herein define the parameters of the Cap Automators.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Cap Automator Target Available Exposure Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Cap Automator Target Available Exposure Definition Core The gap parameter is the target gap between the supply usage and the Supply Cap, in the case of the Supply Cap, or between the borrow usage and the Borrow Cap, in the case of the Borrow Cap.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Cap Automator Cooldown Period Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Cap Automator Cooldown Period Definition Core The ttl parameters is the minimum time requirement before it is possible to increase the Supply Cap or Borrow Cap, expressed in seconds.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Cap Automator Absolute Maximum Exposure Definition Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Cap Automator Absolute Maximum Exposure Definition Core The max parameter is the maximum the Supply Cap or Borrow Cap can be increased to.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Cap Automator Current Configuration Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Cap Automator Current Configuration Core The subdocuments herein define the current configuration of the cap automators for each covered market.
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Cap Automator WETH Parameters Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Cap Automator WETH Parameters Core The current WETH cap automator parameters are:• Supply cap ◦ gap: 150,000 WETH ◦ ttl: 12 hours ◦ max: 2 million WETH• Borrow cap ◦ gap: 10,000 WETH ◦ ttl: 12 hours ◦ max: 1 million WETH
A.3.9 - Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Cap Automator wstETH Parameters Measures For Endgame Transition - SparkLend Risk Parameters - Cap Automator wstETH Parameters Core The current wstETH cap automator parameters are:• Supply cap ◦ gap: 50,000 wstETH ◦ ttl: 12 hours ◦ max: 1.2 million wstETH• Borrow cap ◦ gap: 100 wstETH ◦ ttl: 12 hours ◦ max: 3,000 wstETH
